The Great Tilden 102

— Jiang Huaiqing

Tilden, who devoted his life to tennis, is now forty-two years and nine months old and has never married. When he was performing in Japan, a journalist interviewed him and asked why he didn't marry. Tilden smiled and shook his head, seemingly disapproving of the question, feeling it was meddlesome. Even if marriage would not affect his career, Tilden did not value marriage. Indeed, he had an indissoluble bond with tennis throughout his life.

William T. Tilden 2nd was born on February 10, 1893, in Germanion, Pa, USA. He is about six feet two inches tall and weighs about one hundred and sixty pounds. He began practicing tennis at the age of six and won a boy's medal at the age of seven. It is said to be Tilden's first victory.

Tilden's youth coincided with the flourishing period of lawn tennis in the United States. Influenced by what he saw and heard, coupled with Tilden's special talent, he devoted himself to research, and his tennis skills improved rapidly. In 1918, he reached the final of the U.S. Championships for the first time, and in 1919 he again reached the final, but lost to Johnston. From 1920, he jumped to the U.S. Championships and also won the British Wimbledon Championship, taking the lead in the world. From then on, Tilden's fame shook the world. The following year, he won the Wimbledon Championship for the second time, and from 1922 to 1927 he won the U.S. Championships for six years.

Tilden ranked first in the U.S. Tennis Top Ten for more than ten years (1921-1930) and represented the U.S. in the Davis Cup competition for eleven years (1920-1930). This is a record unmatched by tennis players from other countries. Tilden is known as the eccentric of the tennis world, which is truly fitting. From 1920 to 1926, the United States won the Davis Cup for seven consecutive years, which cannot but be attributed to Tilden, who served as both singles and doubles player and captain. During these years, Tilden maintained the prestige of a winning army and was never defeated by any player. This is even rarer in the tennis world.

Since 1927, the French tennis comets Lacoste and Cochet appeared, and Tilden began to be defeated by these two players. At the same time, the United States also lost the Davis Cup. At that time, Tilden's sharp edge seemed to have withered. According to the usual practice of athletes, Tilden could have put down his butcher knife and let the talented take over, but he did not do so, and instead devoted himself to research even more diligently. At the same time, he began to write tennis books to benefit future generations.

One month before the U.S. and French Davis Cup players were to compete in Paris, Tilden participated in the Wimbledon competition in London (that year Tilden lost to Cochet in the semi-finals). Tilden wrote about the first two weeks of the Wimbledon competition and submitted it to a newspaper in San Francisco for publication. The United States Lawn Tennis Association believed that Tilden's writing about his own participation in the competition was a violation of the amateur sports rules and investigated it several times, resolutely deciding to revoke Tilden's amateur status. Tilden was also the captain of the U.S. Davis Cup team that year, and the association did not allow Tilden to participate in the Davis Cup final. At that time, it caused a sensation around the world and became the first major event in the history of tennis. However, the French tennis community did not take pride in the fact that the opponent in the Davis Cup final had lost its main player and gained the advantage of winning the championship, but resolutely protested to the United States Tennis Association, believing that Tilden did not intentionally violate the amateur rules and should be forgiven. It was also said that the tennis audience across France did not want to lose the opportunity to see the skills of the world's greatest tennis player. This is how countries around the world value sportsmanship and amateur rules. Although Tilden regained his qualifications that year, it gave Tilden the confidence to enter the professional tennis world.

In order to complete the final glory of his life, Tilden took a strong step into the world of professional tennis. He stepped up his practice, tirelessly throughout the year. Sure enough, after completing his third Wimbledon World Championship in 1930, he formally announced his entry into the professional tennis world.

Since joining the professional world, his skills have improved and not declined, and he has traveled to the United States and other countries to compete, which is very hard, but he is full of interest and does not take it to heart. Since recruiting the young tennis player Vines in 1933, the two of them have been an invincible team, truly unmatched in the world. Cochet, the French champion who had repeatedly defeated Tilden before, felt silent and invisible after entering the professional world, far less popular than Tilden and Vines.

In addition to working hard on the court, Tilden also worked hard on writing. He has written more than ten tennis books in his life, and they have all been translated into various languages, truly becoming bestsellers for a time.

Tilden's hitting posture

Local News

A Great Man Bids Farewell Forever, Duan Qirui was Buried Yesterday Afternoon, The Whole Country Flies Flags at Half-Mast for One Day to Express Mourning, President Jiang Sends Mayor Wu to Offer Sacrifices on His Behalf, The Central Government Decides to Give Him a State Funeral 103

The former Provisional Chief Executive Duan Qirui passed away in Shanghai on the 2nd of this month. He was buried yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. The National Government ordered the whole country to fly flags at half-mast to express mourning. In addition to President Jiang specially sending Mayor Wu to offer sacrifices on his behalf, President Yu and Foreign Minister Zhang and others all went to offer condolences. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Arrangement of the Funeral Hall

At the entrance of Duan's residence, a plain-colored archway was built yesterday, with a huge mud-red "Dian" (奠, meaning offering) character embedded in the center, surrounded by electric torches. A tall mat shed was also built on the lawn in front of the funeral hall, paved with wooden boards to serve as a place for guests to rest. The Songhu Garrison Command and the Municipal Public Security Bureau both sent bands to the scene to play mourning music. Duan's former subordinates Li Sihao, Wu Guangxin, Liang Hongzhi, Qu Yingguang, and Zhang Peiyi, etc., all stood in front of the funeral hall to receive guests.

Condolence Personnel

Those who went to Duan's residence to offer condolences yesterday included: President Jiang of the Executive Yuan (represented by Wu Tiecheng), Chairman Wang of the Central Political Committee (represented by Chu Minyi), President Yu Youren of the Control Yuan, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi (represented by his eldest son Ling Kan), Minister of Foreign Affairs Zhang Qun, Mayor of Shanghai Wu Tiecheng, President Chen Diaoyuan of the Military Advisory Council, Education Director Zhang Zhizhong of the Central Military Academy, Songhu Garrison Commander Yang Hu, Central Committee members Tang Shaoyi (represented by Tang Zhu), Li Liejun, Yang Shukan, Zhang Zhiben, Xue Dubi, Chairman Wu Zhongxin of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, Tieci Zeng Rongfu, Japanese Foreign Minister Arita (represented by Wakasugi), Japanese Naval Attaché to China Sato, Assistant Officer Minato, Director Cai Jingjun of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chief Commander Ji Zhangjian of the Security Corps, Deputy Commander Wen Huazhou, Director Zhou Jue of the Diplomatic Office in Shanghai, and You Lie (represented by Ma Baimei), Yao Cong, Qian Xinzhi, Zhou Zuomin, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Xu Xiuzhi, Zhang Xiaolin, Yu Zuoting, Wu Yunzhai, Lu Xuepu, Guo Shun, Zhang Yipeng, Bai Baoshan, Feng Gengguang, Guan Jiongzhi, Wang Changchun, Li Dachao, Funatsu, Luo Gialing, Ji Juemi, Wang Gongtao, and more than 200 former subordinates of Duan.

Situation at the Encoffining

Duan's remains had been encoffined by a technician specially dispatched by the China Funeral Home the day before yesterday. The encoffining took place at 2 p.m. yesterday, and amidst the mourning music and cries, this great man bid farewell to the world forever. The visiting guests, led by Wu Tiecheng, representative of President Jiang, paid their respects one by one and withdrew.

Coffin Placed in Shanghai Residence

Duan's eldest grandson Changshi and second grandson Changren, etc., all arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning by the Shanghai-Pinghu train, accompanied by Duan's son Hongye and nephew Honggang, personally overseeing the encoffining. Duan's coffin will be temporarily placed in the Shanghai residence, and the date and location of the burial are yet to be decided by the central government, as the central government has decided to give Duan a state funeral.

Jiang Sends Another Telegram of Condolence

Chairman Jiang, unable to attend the condolences in person, sent Mayor Wu to offer sacrifices on his behalf and sent another telegram of condolence to Duan Junliang, which read: "Shanghai Mayor Wu translates and forwards to Mr. Duan Junliang. I respectfully received the winter telegram. I sent a telegram of condolence yesterday, which I trust has been delivered. Your respected father has passed away with virtue, and the whole world mourns forever. I am away on duty and cannot attend the encoffining in person. I have entrusted Brother Tiecheng to offer condolences on my behalf and have submitted a request to the government for preferential posthumous honors to show respect and reward. Your filial piety is sincere, and you have suffered such a great loss. I hope you will restrain your grief and cherish yourself, and strive to carry on your father's will. I am deeply concerned. Zhongzheng's secretary, Luo Yin."

Sanbei Buys Four New Ships, First Goes to Hong Kong to Pick Up Ships, Distributing to Various Routes in the River and Sea 106

In order to develop the business of the river and sea routes and adjust the transportation of passengers and goods in the north and south oceans and the Yangtze River, the Sanbei Company has decided to purchase a large number of new ships in addition to the original 30 river and sea ships, so as to expand the Yangtze River and coastal routes. It has been learned that the company has purchased two large seagoing vessels from a British merchant, each with a deadweight of more than 6,000 tons, and two new vessels suitable for navigating the Yangtze River, each with a deadweight of 1,500 tons, and the hull is very good. Negotiations with the shipowners on the purchase contract have been agreed. The total price of the ships is about 700,000 yuan. The company has hired new shipowners and plans to send Yu Shunmao to Hong Kong with the shipowners on the 11th of this month to inspect and accept the four new ships, and then open them to Shanghai, first to the factory for minor repairs, and then send them to navigation, with two giant ships running the outer sea route and two ships running the Yangtze River line.

Page 10

Miscellaneous Grain Industry and Municipal Chamber of Commerce Agreed on Certification, Measures for Domestic Circulation of Grain, Decided to Implement Immediately After Printing Forms and Certificates 110

Xin Sheng News Agency said that Gu Xinyi, chairman of the Miscellaneous Grain Industry Association, has agreed with Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, on the measures for the domestic circulation of national rice, which are certified by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. It is stipulated that all Shanghai miscellaneous grain merchants report to the Industry Association when purchasing rice and grain from the mainland to Shanghai, and when shipping rice and grain from Shanghai to various places. After verification that it is true and there is no private export, the Industry Association requests the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to issue a certificate allowing domestic circulation. The above-mentioned certificates and application forms have been printed by the Industry Association and will be implemented immediately after printing. As for the temporary measures for domestic circulation in Shanghai submitted by the Social Affairs Bureau to the Municipal Government, they do not conflict with the above-mentioned certification measures.

Rice Boats Waiting to be Released. As for the rice boats shipped to Shanghai detained in Jiaxing and Jiashan in Pingyuan, Zhejiang, the rice industry groups in Pinghu and Jiashan have requested the county government to release them after signing a guarantee. However, the rice boats detained in Jiaxing must be released after the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce provides a certificate. Today, the rice boats shipped to Shanghai will definitely not be privately exported, so the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has agreed to issue certificates. However, although the Jiangsu prohibition of grain export measures have been passed, they have not been formally implemented. Shanghai is considered to be outside the territory, so the Miscellaneous Grain Industry Association has requested the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to request Jiangsu Province again not to discriminate against Shanghai and to follow the Zhejiang certification measures in the future.

Prohibition of Export. Regarding the prohibition of grain export, the Shanghai Municipal Government has submitted it to the Central Government for approval. At the same time, the Ministry of Finance invited the Ministry of Industry and the Central Trust Bureau to hold a meeting and handed it over to the Customs Administration to draft measures. Now, Zheng Lai, Director of the Customs Administration, has been ordered by the Ministry to draft measures to prohibit grain export and to investigate the location of grain transportation in detail in order to serve as a reference for drafting measures. According to a leader of the Miscellaneous Grain Industry, the prohibition of grain export is indeed needed in fact, so it is imperative.

Shanghai Rice Prices Fall. After the release of the rice boats shipped to Shanghai that were detained in Jiashan and Pinghu in Zhejiang, the rice boats shipped to Shanghai from various places in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces arrived in Shanghai one after another, and the total amount of rice stored in Shanghai was about 300,000 bags, so the price of rice in Shanghai has fallen again. The real first-class rice has fallen to 11 yuan. There are rumors that about 2,000 bags of rice are shipped from Shanghai to Dalian and the three northeastern provinces every day. According to the news from the Miscellaneous Grain Industry, it is absolutely inaccurate. Moreover, the member rice shops of the association have automatically refused to accept the purchase of foreign merchants.

No More American Ships Will Come to China After the 11th Due to the Impact of the American Sailors' General Strike 111

The Dalai Foreign Company has 19 world-class postal ships operating in the Pacific Ocean and traveling to China. Since the American general strike broke out, the ships that have sailed from the United States to the Far East have been affected. According to a telegram received yesterday, the President Wilson sailed from New York and was still on October 25, before the strike broke out. By the time the ship arrived in Los Angeles on the 2nd of this month, the ship was also prevented from sailing by the strike committee and joined the vortex. The goods inside the ship have been blocked, and passengers can only transfer to non-American ships to come to China. On the Seattle route, the Dalai Foreign Company received a telegram yesterday that only one ship, the President McKinley, was not affected due to the strike because it was already on the Pacific Ocean. The ship is expected to arrive in Japan today, pass Kobe on the 8th, and arrive in Shanghai on the 10th. After the ship arrives in Shanghai, no American ships will sail in the Pacific Ocean. The Grand President, which was scheduled to sail to Shanghai on the next shift, has already gone on strike.

The ships in the Far East that have not been affected by the strike, such as the President Jackson, have already decided to change the route to Victoria, Canada, from today onwards, as the final port, in order to maintain the Sino-American route and protect the traffic on the Pacific line. All goods shipped to the United States and passengers going to the United States will be loaded and unloaded at that port, and then transferred by train to the United States, so as to avoid the American port terminals.

Commercial Registration Law: The Chamber of Commerce Urges Review 112

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of this city, in order to expedite the review of the Commercial Registration Law, submitted a petition to the Legislative Yuan yesterday, stating that the Commercial Registration Law was previously reviewed by a joint meeting of the Commercial Law and Civil Law Committees of your esteemed Yuan on October 31, the 23rd year of the Republic. Our association appointed Li Kuian as a representative to attend. The meeting resulted in the original drafting committee member, Huang Youchang, summarizing the opinions of all parties and revising the draft before submitting it to the two committees for review. Almost two years have passed, and approval has not yet been granted. Our association again, last month, appointed the original representative, Li Kuian, to submit a petition to your esteemed Yuan, urging that a meeting be convened quickly. A reply was received, instructing Huang Youchang to make contact, etc. Li, the representative, went to Beijing on the first of this month and contacted Huang. According to Huang, the draft has been revised and submitted to the Commercial Law and Civil Law Committees, etc. The Commercial Registration Law was originally drafted to remedy Article 681 of the Civil Code. Article 681 of the Civil Code stipulates joint and several liability for partnerships. Disputes arising from this provision are numerous and unbearable, causing good people to be unwilling to invest more and cunning people to use it as a shield. This situation, we believe, has long been within the purview of your esteemed Yuan, hence the separate drafting of the Commercial Registration Law as a remedy. Now, its invisible stagnation is likely not your esteemed Yuan's original intention. It is appropriate to submit another petition to your esteemed Yuan for review, earnestly requesting that you promptly urge the two committees to convene a meeting for review at a set time and allow our association to send representatives to attend, as this is extremely important. Respectfully, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce.

One Year of the New Currency Law: Achievements: Stable Exchange Rates, Solid International Credit, Relaxed Market, and Optimistic Prospects for the Recovery of Various Industries 117

According to the New News Agency, our country's New Currency Law was promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Finance on November 4th of last year. November 4th of this year marks its first anniversary. In this year, our country's financial situation has made great progress, and the national economy is gradually recovering. The prospects are quite optimistic. The New News Agency reporter reports on various situations as follows:

(Stable Exchange Rates) Although the New Currency Law has only been implemented for one year, the results achieved in various aspects are already quite impressive. In terms of financial construction, in addition to the centralized issuance and consolidation of currency, the most significant achievement is the stabilization of exchange rates and the consolidation of international credit. To ensure the stability of exchange rates, the Ministry of Finance increased foreign exchange reserves, stabilized exchange rates, and ordered the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of China to restrict the trading of foreign exchange, using the financial strength of the state to establish a foundation for foreign exchange. As a result, the market price of our country's foreign exchange has been able to consistently stand at around one shilling and two and a half pence, and the center of gravity has shifted towards us.

(Market Recovery) In order to rescue the market, the Ministry of Finance ordered various banks to increase the amount of loans, regulate rural credit, implement a low-interest rate policy, and issue 146 million yuan in unified government bonds to repay domestic government bonds, treasury bills, and certificates issued by the government over the years. It also issued 34 million yuan in reconstruction government bonds to complete the legal tender policy, improve financial organization, and support production and construction. At the same time, it ordered the Shanghai silver industry to study methods to reduce interest rates. As a result, market interest rates have been slightly lower on average than in previous years. In addition, the urgency of the Spring Festival, the Dragon Boat Festival at the end of April, and the recent financial season at the end of October in the Shanghai market this year has been much more relaxed than a year ago, and the Shanghai interbank lending rate has remained unusually stable, and various industries are gradually recovering.

Guanglong Line Changed to Guangyong Line; Also Heard of Guanghe Line 118

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1368 states: Approved Southwest Airlines' telegram to change the Guanglong line from Guangzhou, via Wuzhou, Guilin, and Liuzhou, to Yongning, no longer flying to Longzhou, and renamed the Guangyong line. The weekly flights are Mondays, Wednesdays, Fridays, and Saturdays upwards, and Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays downwards. However, at the beginning of the change of the route, only two flights will be operated per week on Mondays and Wednesdays. As for the original Guanglong line, it has long been extended to Hanoi, from Guangzhou via Wuzhou, Yongning, and Longzhou to Hanoi, now renamed the Guanghe line, to match the name with the reality. The weekly flights are Fridays westwards and Saturdays eastwards. The change of the air route will be implemented from November 4th, etc. Accordingly, a notice is hereby issued for general information. This is the announcement, Director Zha Peilin.

Shanghai-Shaanxi Line Zhengping Section Flight Time Advanced 119

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation Shanghai-Shaanxi Line Zhengping Section route, originally scheduled to fly north from Zhengzhou at 2:00 PM every Thursday and Sunday, was scheduled to arrive in Beiping at 5:30 PM, connecting with the route flying east from Lanzhou at 8:00 AM that morning. It is now known that in northern winter, the sun sets around 4:00 PM, and the Beiping airport does not yet have night navigation equipment. Therefore, starting from the 1st of this month, the northward flight on this section has been changed to 8:00 AM every Monday and Friday, arriving in Beiping at 11:00 AM. There has been no change in the flight time from Beiping to Zhengzhou.

Peruvian Min Xing Daily: Li Jiyuan Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday: Overseas Chinese Business Economic Situation is Good 120

According to the Central News Agency, Li Jiyuan, editor-in-chief of the Min Xing Daily in Peru, South America, returned to China aboard the President Lincoln yesterday morning, arriving in Shanghai. A reporter visited him and inquired about the current situation of overseas Chinese. According to him, Peru was the first country in the Americas to trade with China. In the past, there were tens of thousands of overseas Chinese, but now there are about 10,000, of which more than 2,000 are members of the Kuomintang. The overseas Chinese in that area are more knowledgeable than the locals, and they are all engaged in commerce. In recent years, the economic situation has been better than in the past. However, education is not very developed, and some children do not even know Cantonese, let alone the written language of the motherland. In the past, Mr. Chen Lifu encouraged the establishment of schools and promised to donate books. Now, three schools have been established, and the situation has greatly changed. Overseas Chinese in North and South America are extremely excited about the unification of the country. When Yu Hanmou's telegram arrived, they cheered wildly, especially expressing their great love and admiration for President Chiang Kai-shek for his hard work and great achievements. Overseas Chinese have always been bullied by foreigners, and now they are very happy to see their motherland striving to make progress.

British Troops Relieved Yesterday 121

Around 7:00 AM yesterday, the British 11,000-ton transport ship Dilwara arrived in Shanghai from England, carrying the 2nd Battalion of the North Lancashire Regiment, and docked at the Hongkou Wharf. Around 9:30 AM, the soldiers of the battalion disembarked, marching along Nanjing Road to the Racecourse. At the same time, the 2nd Battalion of the Lancashire Fusiliers, stationed in Shanghai, marched out of the barracks on Great Western Road and entered the Racecourse. Brigadier General Smart, commander of the British troops stationed in Shanghai, received the salute of the entering and exiting battalions in front of the Country Club. The two battalions gathered at the Racecourse for about half an hour, shaking hands and exchanging cigarettes and news from China and England. Then they separated. The newly arrived troops went directly to the barracks on Great Western Road, while the troops originally stationed in Shanghai went to the riverside to board the transport ship, which will sail to Tianjin this morning to be stationed there. Many people watched along the way this morning, and the U.S. Marine Corps band stationed in Shanghai escorted them.

Pu River Launches Towing Ships: Changed to Two-Row Navigation: Harbor Master and Inland River Ship Association: Purely for Navigation Safety 130

Harbor Master Tebeck of the Jianghai Customs, in order to maintain the safety of ships sailing on the Pu River, has specially stipulated that vessels towed by tugboats should change from a single row to a double row, which was promulgated in Announcement No. 15 last month. The Inland River Ship Industry Association of this city believes that towing according to the old rules has been practiced for a long time and has not caused any danger. Now that various ship bureaus find the new method difficult, they specially sent a letter to the Customs on the 24th of last month, requesting permission to continue towing in a single row. The association received a reply from Harbor Master Tebeck No. 27083 yesterday, stating that according to the request of Yuantong Steamship Company and others, if the barges are towed according to the regulations in Article 3 of Announcement No. 15 of this office, it would be inconvenient and dangerous for navigation. It should be requested that the reply be forwarded for approval of amendment. Upon investigation, the reasons for opposition stated in the letter are not approved by this office. Regarding the first point, "Tugboats and barges are attacked by the current from three sides as soon as they exit the Suzhou Creek." Tugboats are only subject to the impact of the current from one side of the rising or falling tide at any time they exit the Suzhou Creek, and there is no situation of being attacked from three sides. Therefore, if the tugboat gradually advances against the current, changing the tow from a single row to a double row will not cause difficulties. Regarding the second point, "The size and height of the barges are different," the shape and size of the barges are completely unrelated to the arrangement of the tugs. It is only necessary to separate the middle of the barges towed in parallel with guard rails to avoid accidents. Moreover, the method of towing barges side by side is not unique to this port. It is common practice in various ports in the country and around the world. For example, large and small iron barges in this port tow garbage ships or fishing boats, often in three rows, with three or four boats towed in each row. This is seen every day, and there has been no difficulty. As for the third point, "There are many other ships in the Suzhou Creek," this is irrelevant to whether the tugboats are in a single or double row. In short, changing the barges from a single row to a double row is only somewhat inconvenient in terms of procedure, but there is no danger to the barges being towed. Moreover, the Bund Park corner is an extremely dangerous area in this port where ships are particularly crowded. It seems that this fundamental issue should be weighed against the above-mentioned inconvenient procedures. When this office planned the change, it carefully considered that the danger of navigation in the port is purely due to the excessive length of the barges. To protect the safety of ships, two methods were originally planned: one is to reduce the number of barges to shorten their length, and the other is to change the barges to a double row. The second method can make it unnecessary to reduce the number of barges and will not affect the business of various inland river ships. Therefore, it was decided to adopt and implement it. If the members of your association wish to follow the first method, that is, to tow a total of three vessels in a row, that is also possible. It should be known that the change in the method of towing by small barges is purely for safety considerations by this office. In the past twenty years, the situation in this port has changed, and the number of ships entering and leaving has increased day by day. The old regulations must be improved appropriately. I hope that your association, which is enthusiastic about public welfare, will assist in this matter. This reply is hereby made for your information.

Social Affairs Bureau Orders Schools to Conduct X-Ray Examinations for Staff and Students 132

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau recently instructed all levels of schools in the city, stating that the Dean of the Private Tongde Medical College, Gu Yuqi, reported that in view of the importance of public health and the urgent need to promote tuberculosis prevention, the college decided to conduct tuberculosis prevention X-ray examinations. To popularize the examinations, a handling fee of only one yuan was charged per person per examination; for middle school students, the fee was only eight jiao per examination, and for primary school students, the fee was six jiao. From September 1st to the end of September, a total of 428 people came to the college for examinations, including 96 students. Among them, eight students had been cured of lung disease, and seventeen were in the early stages, accounting for approximately 20% of the students. This phenomenon among a small number of students is truly alarming. The college originally focused on the examination of school students and faculty. Now that the number of students is small, and none of the faculty members have been examined, it is necessary to actively promote this work. It is requested that the Bureau issue another order to all levels of schools in the city to uniformly implement the examination to emphasize public health and prevent disease. The details of the examination have been compiled into a table and submitted for review and record. This is in the public interest. Two copies of the form are attached. Based on this, the college had previously requested the former Municipal Education Bureau to order all levels of schools to implement X-ray examinations of students' lungs. Now, based on the previous situation, it is urgently requested that the schools strictly comply with the order. This order is issued by Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Bureau.

Transportation Tugboat Damages Two Vegetable Boats; Total Loss of 1,000 Yuan 135

Qian Jinchun, a Jiangbei sand boat carrying 500 heads of cabbage, came to Songjiang for sale. When it arrived near the Shigeng area of Wusongkou, another boat named Xue Kui, also carrying 300 heads of cabbage, came to Songjiang. The two vegetable boats were sailing side by side and entering the port at the same time when a tugboat named Ying Wan, owned by the Japanese Sanlin Transportation Company, towing a barge, came from the Yangtze River to Shanghai. When it arrived at Shigeng, it moved forward between the two vegetable boats. Due to carelessness, it crashed into the bow of the Xue Kui boat, causing significant damage. Fortunately, other cargo ships nearby helped them to the shallows. Yesterday morning, they hired a small tugboat to tow them to Wusong to report the incident. The incident was reported to the tax firm Xujinji and the pig industry customs clearance office, who submitted a report to Zhang Hua, the Haiguan Hebo Division, requesting the tax authorities to negotiate compensation with the transportation company. It is reported that the total loss of the two vegetable boats is about 1,000 yuan.

53 Fashion Shops' Workers Went on Strike Yesterday Morning; Employers and Foremen Reduced Wages; Workers' Representatives Petitioned Yesterday 136

Dagong News reported that all fashion workers went on strike on October 17, 1933, due to a wage dispute. Subsequently, employers and the Garment Workers' Union signed six labor-management agreements. The wage section stipulated that the price for each coat was three yuan, the price for skirts (straight hem, uniformly called) was two yuan and twenty cents, the price for raincoats was one yuan, the price for capes was two yuan and twenty cents, the price for leather coats was three yuan, and the price for petticoats was thirty cents (extra for colored ones). The agreements were filed with the Party and government authorities, and the labor dispute was resolved. However, the wage agreement stipulated that the price for each coat was three yuan, with the worker receiving two yuan and sixty cents, and the foreman receiving forty cents. Unexpectedly, at the beginning of the autumn business season this year, the foremen paid the workers only one yuan and sixty or seventy cents per piece, with the foremen taking the difference. The employers also took the opportunity to reduce wages, and the fashion shops followed suit, unwilling to fulfill their obligations under the labor-management agreement.

Full strike

After the employers and foremen reduced wages, the union reported the situation to the Municipal Party Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting mediation. The Social Affairs Bureau summoned both labor and management representatives to the Bureau for mediation on September 29th and October 30th. The first time, the representatives of the Western Clothing Industry Association attended on behalf of the employers, but no results were achieved. The second time, they refused to attend, making mediation impossible. This caused widespread dissatisfaction, and suddenly, yesterday morning, all 700 workers from 53 fashion shops in the area of Fourth Avenue and Daxin Street, including Dahua, Huamei, Taixing, Datong, Zhongxing, Dachina, New China, Limei, Daxin, and Huaxin, went on strike.

Workers Petition

After all the workers went on strike, at 9:00 AM, they sent representatives Xu Guizhen, Chai Liangfa, Su Changjin, Zhang Yong'an, and Wang Xunqi, together with more than 50 worker representatives from 53 fashion shops, to petition various agencies such as the Municipal Party Committee, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the General Labor Union. Lu Yinchu, Wang Xianqing, and Wan Banghe received them separately. After the representatives explained the meaning of the petition, the Party and government representatives summoned both labor and management representatives to conduct mediation, hoping that the representatives would persuade the workers to wait for a legal solution to avoid expanding the dispute. The representatives were satisfied and returned.

Case of Counterfeiting Hubei Subsidiary Coin Notes; Court of Appeals Rendered a Verdict; Initial Trial Sentenced to Five Years; Yesterday's Appeal Sentenced to Eight Years 137

Lu Fangzheng, a doctor from Hubei, was found to have counterfeited the Hubei Provincial Bank's letter of authorization. Liu Peiqing, the owner of a carving company at No. 20, Lane 153, Baige Road, carved 100,000 five-jiao subsidiary coin notes of the Hubei Provincial Bank. After the case was discovered, the Xinzha police arrested Lu and handed him over to the First Special District Court. After interrogation, Lu Fangzheng was sentenced to five years in prison. The police, believing that this kind of counterfeiting disrupted the financial system and that the crime was serious, and that the initial trial's sentence of only five years was insufficient to deter others, had their lawyer, Tian Yin, appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. After the interrogation was completed, yesterday afternoon, Chief Justice Yu Hua, together with Justices Hua and Zhou, announced the verdict: the original verdict was revoked, and Lu Fangzheng was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment for the intention to supply counterfeit currency for use. The 100,000 counterfeit Hubei Provincial Bank notes, a set of samples, eight engraving plates, two engraving molds, a contract, a copy of the certification, and the counterfeit letters and seals were all confiscated.

Lin Gendi insisted that she, Mao, and Jiang killed Cai Ying, a No. 1 waitress at Daxin Company, in a pavilion room at No. 3 Cunfu Lane, Bapaoluo Road, on August 5th. Although Jiang Yuantan had once admitted it, he later retracted his confession. Mao Agen simply denied it. Although the trial judge Zhong Qing and Mao Agen's lawyer Fan Gang tried their best to investigate, they could not obtain conclusive evidence on the following points: (1) Whether there was a person named Cai Ying at No. 3 Cunfu Lane; (2) Whether there was a waitress named Cai Ying at Daxin Company; (3) Whether Cai Ying, whom Lin Gendi confessed to killing, was the corpse in the box. Lawyer Fan had gone to various places to investigate the above points, but to no avail, making the case

Mysterious and Unpredictable. On the 20th of last month, Judge Zhong, having exhausted his investigative abilities, ordered the debate and declared the conclusion of the case, setting a time for the verdict. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Police Lawyer Zhang Zhizhu and Mao Agen's Lawyer Fan Gang were in court waiting for the verdict. At about 5:00 PM, Judge Zhong Qing and Prosecutor Zhang Zongru took their seats in the third criminal court and announced the verdict. The main text of the verdict stated that Lin Gendi, Mao Agen, and Jiang Yuantan were all not guilty, and also announced

The reason for the verdict, which stated in brief that, according to the witness's testimony, Lin, the president of the company, Lin Gendi told someone at the intersection of Carter Road that after killing Cai Ying, she cut off both hands. However, Lin also stated during the court hearing that both hands were cut off. But the discovered corpse, according to the autopsy results, did not have both hands cut off. Thus, Lin's confession was obviously inconsistent with the facts, and there were many doubts in the case, making it difficult to make a guilty verdict. However, this case

Involves serious circumstances. It is hoped that the police will appeal. At the appeal hearing, or new evidence may be discovered, and a fair and appropriate judgment may be obtained. Police Lawyer Zhang immediately expressed his willingness to consider it, but requested that the defendants be remanded in custody during the appeal period. Lawyer Fan Gang requested that Mao be allowed to be released on bail. Judge Zhong stated that the case was serious and that bail could not be granted before a final verdict was made. Therefore, he ordered that Lin, Mao, and Jiang be remanded in custody during the appeal period.

Xu Wancheng Accuses Luo Tong, etc., to the Jiangsu High Court 148

Xu Wancheng, an editor at the Shanghai News Bookstore, was detained for a long time for commenting on a case in the Shanghai Local Court. Xu accused the judicial administrative department, and the judicial administrative department approved the accusation to the Jiangsu High Court. Xu's case has now attracted the attention of society. The original text of the accusation to the Jiangsu High Court is copied below: "Submitting an accusation that the former President of the Shanghai Local Court, Luo Tong, and Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu, and Judge Lu Hongze, have acted with disdain for the law, abused their authority, and illegally detained me for nearly two and a half months, causing me to suffer greatly, and requesting

Investigation according to law to safeguard national law." The Judicial Administration Department approved the accusation to the court in Document No. 2964. "I graduated from Jiangsu Provincial Second Normal School (formerly Longmen Normal School, now renamed Shanghai Provincial High School) and Datong University, majoring in education. I have always advocated that the education sector must set an example, and the judicial sector must rectify itself. I deeply admire Chairman Chiang's efforts to clean up officialdom. I deeply feel that China's foreign troubles are urgent because of the failure to repair internal affairs. To repair internal affairs, we must first clean up officialdom, and then the country can be governed. Looking around the domestic situation, I feel sad. Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners live together, and the eyes of the world are on us. The national system depends on this. The former President of the Shanghai Local Court, Luo Tong, has been in office for less than a year, and there have been

Many Things to Criticize. For example, the stolen (?) pistol has been a laughing stock among friendly nations. If the Public Security Bureau and the police station themselves have theft, what will the public opinion of the people be like? Article 130 of the Criminal Law states that 'Public officials who neglect their duties and cause disasters shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years but not more than ten years.' If the court can have a stolen pistol, is it not a dereliction of duty? Spreading this new type of pistol into society will cause many crimes. Is this not causing disaster? I heard that Luo Tong is about to be transferred to the Hubei Higher Branch Court. If so, is the national legislation only for the common people? I do not want to say it, and I cannot bear to say it. Since Luo Tong has been the President of the Court, there have been cases of prosecutors and judges being bribed and reported and punished. I will not discuss others, but even just the ones that have been discovered are heartbreaking. In short, during Luo Tong's

Presidency, the Shanghai citizens were angry and dared not speak out. I am honest and straightforward by nature, and out of righteous indignation, I wrote an article commenting on the situation. All of them are based on facts, and there are witnesses. There is no malice in what I said. The purpose is to promote the judiciary. I did not expect to offend the anger of these people, who considered it an insult and slander. The President ordered Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu to open a second court investigation on the afternoon of June 8th of this year. I was summoned and arrived, but was still detained. On the morning of the 13th of the same month, the trial judge Lu Hongze's attitude was irritable and biased. He made it clear that he was prejudiced. I was unwilling to give a confession and requested a change of jurisdiction and bail. The judge verbally stated that bail would not be granted, fearing that if I were released on bail, I would

Continue to commit crimes. The judge had not inquired about the case in detail, but had already determined that the defendant was guilty. This is extremely absurd. I was detained for nearly two and a half months. In the small room of the detention center, there were more than ten people imprisoned. It was summer, the heat was unbearable, and the bedbugs and white worms were swarming day and night. The environment was terrible. I

Was Seriously Ill. I reported it for treatment, but it was ignored. Judge Lu Hongze did not allow bail. In his ruling, he falsely accused my illness of being fabricated, which is especially hateful. Furthermore, hot water was not always provided in the detention center. My family was often prevented from delivering necessary items and food, and all kinds of abuses were inflicted on me. If I were to describe them one by one, I could not exhaust them in ten million words. I am devoted to education and cultural undertakings. After being detained, everything was left unattended. I was anxious to die, and was forced by internal and external pressures.

Every Day Felt Like a Year. This kind of suffering cannot be described in words. Fortunately, President Lu Xinhuai was magnanimous and personally investigated and discovered that I was seriously ill, with my feet rotting and my face swollen. I was dying. He ordered me to be sent to the hospital for treatment, which can be verified. My body has not yet recovered from the illness. I have been stimulated too deeply, and both eyes have become incurable. I am still alive, which is fortunate. Later, I appealed to the court, and the order was given to make a new legal ruling. However, the judge delayed it for many days. I had no choice but to appeal to the new President again for relief, and I was granted bail. However, all kinds of difficulties were added during the bail process. In short, the previous situation of this case, after reading the case file, about my thesis and confession, and the prosecutor's indictment, and the judge's

Ruling Not to Grant Bail, and newspaper reports, etc., can prove whether there was abuse of power and illegal detention. The Wuxian District Court has now concluded the case, and the case is clear. At most, it is a fine of 30 yuan and a suspended sentence of two years. In such a minor case, I was detained from 2:30 PM on June 8th to 11:15 AM on August 22nd, a total of 72 days, 21 hours, and 15 minutes. May I ask what is it if it is not acting with disregard for the law, abusing power, and detaining illegally? Former President Luo Tong, Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu, and Judge Lu Hongze have violated Articles 125, Paragraph 1 and Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. If they are not severely punished, it is feared that others will follow suit. The authority and integrity of the judiciary should start from itself. The credibility of the Shanghai Local Court in the past

Had Long Been Lost. Instead of rectifying the situation, they want to silence the people and detain me on false pretenses. (In his reply to Shi Jun of the National Government, Luo Tong expressed his hatred for me in writing, which can be used as evidence.) This further shows their baseness. The laws and regulations of the country are collapsing. My personal loss is still small. Therefore, the judiciary itself should be strictly corrected to maintain the spirit of legislation. For the sake of the overall situation and for the sake of maintaining the national legal system, I will not be silent. Therefore, in accordance with the approval of the Judicial Administration Department, I am filing a complaint with the court, respectfully requesting investigation and legal handling. Furthermore, during this detention, former President Luo Tong and Judges Tang Ruxiu and Lu Hongze arbitrarily detained me, which was close to hostile behavior. All losses, such as medical expenses and various losses during detention, should be compensated by the three defendants to punish the unruly. I am a poor man in Jiangsu and seek relief. Your merit will be immeasurable. Sincerely, Xu Wancheng, Jiangsu High Court. Attach a copy of the Judicial Administration Department's approval and evidence.

Fishmonger Bored to the Extreme: Married off Wife in a Scheme, Pretending to Be Father and Daughter to Collect Betrothal Gifts and then Eloping After the Wedding; Fishmonger Visited the Groom, Treating Him to Wine and Meat, and Both Eloped Home After a Feast; All Involved Were Arrested After the Case Was Exposed 151

Jin Guocheng (also known as Wang Jinsheng), a local resident, 49 years old, is a fishmonger residing at No. 220, Lane 162, Changping Li, You Dai Jiao. On April 11th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, he married Wu Lude, a woman from his hometown, whom he obtained from the Jiliang Institute. She is currently 24 years old. Last September, they had a child. Recently, due to the dwindling source of fishmonger's livelihood and financial constraints, he colluded with a man named Miao Ruikui, who is currently at large, to carry out a plan to

arrange a "pigeon marriage." A Ningbo man named Lu Weisheng, 35 years old, residing at No. 45, Renchang Li, Qiwupu Road, works as a shop assistant at Hujiang University on Yangshupu Road and is still single. He entrusted old women from his hometown, Shen A'da and Lin A'lin, to look for a cheap village woman for him, regardless of her appearance. Miao and Jin learned of this opportunity and, through the help of a woman named Shi Wu, contacted Lu Weisheng's widowed sister-in-law, Ma. The two Ningbo women, Shen A'da and Lin A'lin, took Jin's wife to Lu's house. Little uncle Weisheng

found her agreeable and agreed to a betrothal gift of 120 yuan. He also met with Jin Guocheng, who claimed that his wife was his eldest daughter and that because he was old, he needed to quickly marry her off to take care of her for the rest of her life. Lu was overjoyed and chose an auspicious day, September 27th, to give the betrothal gift of 120 yuan to the matchmakers Shen A'da and Lin A'lin, who handed it over to Jin Guocheng, who accepted it and made a written receipt. Jin used the alias Wang Jinsheng, Wu changed her name to Wang Xiaomei, and they temporarily abandoned the child,

disguised as a bride, and took a car to Lu's house. She and Weisheng kowtowed to heaven and earth and consummated their marriage, while the groom was completely in the dark, unaware of the "pigeon marriage" scheme. On the afternoon of the 25th of last month, Jin Guocheng went to Lu Weisheng's house, pretending to visit his daughter. Lu treated him as his father-in-law, providing wine and meat for lunch. Around 2 p.m., while Lu went out shopping, Jin and his wife eloped back home, hiding in their bedroom,

to listen for news. Lu Weisheng returned home and found his bride missing. He searched everywhere, but to no avail. He then reported the situation to the Yulin Road Patrol House. Hua Detective Liu Zhisheng arrested Jin at a tiger stove on Changping Road at 7 a.m. the day before yesterday and also found Wu at his home. Both were taken back to the patrol house,

detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. A lawyer from the Bureau of Public Works, Zhang Shizhu, explained the case and requested an investigation. The marriage certificate was presented for inspection. Subsequently, Lu Weisheng, the matchmakers Shen A'da and Lin A'lin, Lu Ma, Shi Wu, and others testified about the events. When questioned, both defendants stammered. Judge Zhong Qing ordered them to be remanded in custody pending sentencing.

Recently, traffic accidents involving buses in the city have been frequent, with statistics from the French Concession showing an average of over 85 cases per day, which is alarming. In the case of Zhou A'mao, an apprentice at an American fruit store, being run over and killed by a British public bus at the intersection of Haig Road and Diefeng Road on the 28th of last month, Zhou Shengcai, the father of the victim, has entrusted lawyer Wang Jian'e to file a lawsuit according to law. Yesterday, he also submitted petitions to the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession, the Citizens' United Association, and the Ningbo Association in Shanghai, requesting them to negotiate with the company for compensation and to punish the driver involved in the accident. The original petition stated: "I, Zhou Shengcai, am 63 years old, from Zhenhai, residing in Dingxing Li, North Sichuan Road. My only son was tragically killed by a speeding British public bus. I implore you to seek justice. My son A'mao, 18 years old, was an apprentice at the American fruit store at No. 1253 Jing'an Temple Road. On the 28th of this month, he was delivering goods by bicycle. Around 12:15 p.m., while traveling east to west through the intersection of Haig Road and Diefeng Road, a British public bus (driven by Zheng Changyou, No. 427, from Jiangbei) sped forward without honking its horn, causing my son's bicycle to be unable to avoid it. He was knocked to the ground, and the driver, knowing that he had caused an accident, still did not brake, intending to escape punishment. It was not until the patrolman noticed (after being dragged for three yards) and ordered him to stop that he finally braked. However, my son was already under the bus, his left and right ribs were crushed, he was unconscious, and he was spitting blood. Patrolman No. 3002 and passersby lifted the bus and pulled him out, sending him to the Red Cross General Hospital, but it was too late to save him, and he died tragically. Because the accident occurred at the intersection of the French Concession and the Chinese-administered area, the French police ordered detectives to investigate the incident, and the Second Special Court verified that the death was indeed the case. My wife and I are both over sixty years old and relied on this only son for our livelihood. Now that he has been tragically killed, how can we survive? Therefore, I specially appeal to your associations to uphold justice, write to the Second Special Court to severely punish the bus driver for his disregard for human life, and write to the company to negotiate compensation so that I can barely survive. I respectfully submit this petition."

The sanatorium is located in a quiet place with fresh air, and the ward equipment is perfect, with attentive nursing, which is most suitable for patients to recuperate. He intends to stay for another week before being discharged and returning home. He praised the doctors and nurses of the sanatorium for their ability to do their best and was very grateful. The reporter saw that there were many hospitals in Shanghai, but few hospitals could satisfy people's wishes. Seeing other patients in the sanatorium, either resting quietly or walking around, if it were not for the name "sanatorium," one would almost suspect that this was a high-class hotel for avoiding disasters.

Embezzlement Case of Yong'an Company Furniture Department Employee Concludes Yesterday. Defendant Claims Meager Salary and Heavy Family Burden; Truly Left with No Choice but to Commit this Illegal Act 171

Chen Ding'an from Ningbo and Wang Jiegui from Shanghai, etc., were employees in the furniture department of Yong'an Company on Nanjing Road. However, according to the company's regulations, when employees of various departments are busy with their duties and have no time to eat, they can obtain a signed paper from their respective department heads to claim a meal allowance of four jiao. Chen et al. exploited this system by using department heads' signed slips and fabricating pretexts to fraudulently obtain funds from the company's accounting department for their own use. On the 25th of last month, Chen Ding'an continued to use this method, writing a slip intending to fraudulently claim 135 yuan, but was discovered. The case was reported to the Laozha Police Station, which ordered detective He Renrui to arrest Chen Ding'an and Wang Jiegui, along with suspect Qing Lingen, and send them to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Ye Shengchao took his seat in the Second Criminal Court for further interrogation. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu rose and stated the case, saying that during the adjournment, the police found that Ying Lingen was not involved in the case and should be released first. However, Chen Ding'an and Wang Jiegui had repeatedly used this method to defraud the company's accounting department, and it was not a one-time occurrence. Moreover, Wang Jiegui also used his position to not sell the company's goods to customers, but instead resold woodenware from Dachang and Yuanchang in Ningbo Road to buyers, thereby harming the company's rights. He requested a strict investigation and severe punishment. The legal representative of Yong'an Company, Guo Wenhui, head of the furniture department, also hired lawyers Xu Shihao and Zuo Dejin to appear in court, filing a civil suit claiming 975 yuan from Chen Ding'an and 122.20 yuan from Wang Jiegui, requesting recovery and a joint judgment. When questioned, Chen Ding'an confessed to the charges, saying, "I have been working in the furniture department of Yong'an Company for more than ten years. My monthly salary is only about 20 yuan. I still have an elderly father and wife to support at home. This is barely enough to survive. Last year, my grandmother passed away, so I was left with no choice but to commit this illegal act. I beg for leniency on this point." When questioned, Wang Jiegui did not admit to the crime. After the lawyers for both parties debated, Judge Ye ordered that the case be adjourned until next Tuesday for the pronouncement of judgment. The two defendants were remanded in custody, and Ying Lingen was released.

The evolving environment and situation made it impossible to predict whether and how future changes might occur. Bullish sentiment was relatively strong on the exchange, but there were no opportunities to seize, and the market remained in a temporary state of stagnation. Throughout the day, the market initially weakened due to significant selling of the No. 43 bond, with prices generally falling by small amounts ranging from 0.05 to 0.25 yuan. Margin trading only saw slight swap activity, and the market stabilized, with early issues showing slight weakness and later issues showing slight firmness, fluctuating by only about 0.10 yuan. The afternoon opening saw the situation remain relatively firm. Early issues were slightly weaker, while later issues were relatively firmer. The closing initially showed flat weakness, but later issues remained stable. Ultimately, due to more short selling swaps, near-term bonds fell by about 0.10 yuan and long-term bonds fell by about 0.20 yuan. However, near-term Type A bonds and long-term Type B bonds were slightly better by 0.05 to 0.10 yuan to compensate for the previous day's deficiencies. The total transaction volume was only 2,915,000 yuan. The resulting price changes are listed in the table on the left. (Unit: yuan, Transaction Unit: 100 yuan)

Grains Foreign Barley Quotes Rise, Futures Flour and Wheat Both Rise, Flour Up 0.03 to 0.05 Yuan, Wheat Jumps About 0.10 Yuan 183

Flour: Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market, the prices of all months showed a strong rebound. The price of foreign barley rose by 0.20 yuan in Chicago, and Canadian barley rose by 0.06 to 0.07 yuan. Liverpool rose by 1 pence. Therefore, after the opening, the sentiment for both near-term and long-term contracts became bullish again. Near-term contracts rose by 0.02 to 0.03 yuan, while long-term contracts rose by 0.04 to 0.05 yuan. This was because the previous day's decline had been excessive, and yesterday's foreign barley rebounded strongly. Therefore, outside buyers competed to buy in, and the market atmosphere recovered vigorously. By the afternoon opening, the market was still firm, but then bulls sold out, and new buyers were hesitant. The market turned flat and weak again. Looking ahead, because the market value has reached its peak, it will be difficult to see further gains without actual sales driving the market.

Wheat: Yesterday, the futures wheat market suddenly rose sharply in all months after the morning opening, because the price of foreign barley immediately rebounded by 0.20 to 0.06-0.07 yuan. The sharp decline the previous day inevitably led to a review. Furthermore, the market is now focused on changes in the international situation. Because domestic wheat is in short supply, the increase in inventory will inevitably depend on foreign barley. Therefore, the sentiment rose with the price of foreign barley, rising by about 0.10 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. The afternoon opening was initially stable, but then the current month's contract fell by 0.02 yuan due to bulls selling out. Long-term contracts remained stable. Spot wheat prices remained fixed as customers offered sales. Shanfu Xinban had 2,000 bags, and Shen Da had 500 bags.

Rice Sales Remain Sluggish 184

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, about 40 boats arrived from the lower reaches of the river. Sales of various goods in the market remained sluggish. The price of new japonica rice fell by a small margin, and the price of thin indica rice also showed a soft trend, following a slight decline of 0.01 to 0.02 yuan in early trading. Baiyuan also saw a slight decline, while high-quality Yinyuan rice remained stable, with medium and low grades showing sluggish transactions. Various indica rice varieties saw weak sales, with prices trending downward. All other goods also showed a soft trend.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of goods was slightly scarce, with a total of 37 or 38 boats arriving, carrying a total of over 8,000 shi of goods. Sales in the local market were average. Bag merchants, including Pingjin Biaoyan and other groups, purchased over 2,000 bags of new japonica rice and over 4,000 bags of thin indica rice. Therefore, the market situation for thin indica rice did not improve, and prices rose by 0.05 yuan. Thick new japonica rice only remained stable. Looking at the overall trend, thin indica rice may have a chance of continuing to rise if the supply source does not become strong again. Du indica rice saw no gains or losses. Foreign sharp rice sales were sluggish and showed a soft trend. New Yinyuan rice was mediocre, and new Bianyuan rice alone fell by 0.10 yuan because the opening price was too high.

Rough Indica Rice Guangdong Continues to Purchase Over 7,000 Bags 185

Yesterday, over 10,000 bags of guest indica rice continued to arrive. Due to sluggish sales in recent days, the market situation continued to soften. The market atmosphere was very weak in the morning. Subsequently, guest merchants took advantage of the small market and inquired. As the weather turned sunny, the number of buyers also became slightly more active. The previous purchases by Guangdong merchants were nearly loaded, and yesterday they also purchased over 7,000 bags of various rough rice varieties. Henan merchants also actively purchased late Jing rice. Local Shantou and Ningbo merchants also inquired, and the market finally stabilized. However, the market has been soft for a long time, and there is a large amount of inventory. Although guest sales are active, market prices have not risen. Throughout the day, 6,281 bags of Jiangxi rice, 6,100 bags of Hunan rice, 300 bags of Hubei rice, and 246 bags of Ningbo and Taizhou rice were sold.

Sugar Market Ordinary Cotton and Red Sugar Prices Remain Flat 186

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was stable. The guild set the price for No. 24 coarse granulated white spot goods at 21.65 yuan, but no transactions were made. Re-export goods fell slightly by 0.05 yuan to 6.05 yuan. Only No. 8 white spot goods (N mark) were traded at 21.40 yuan, while the rest remained unchanged. The price of cotton from this factory, Jin Xin No. 1, was 20.50 yuan, No. 2 was 20.30 yuan, No. 3 was 20.10 yuan, No. 4 was 19.90 yuan, and No. 5 was 19.70 yuan. There were also no significant changes. Only the Chaozhou merchants offered prices for bag-packed ordinary cotton and red sugar, with several hundred bags priced at 14.45 to 14.50 yuan. Because the cost of Chaoqing sugar was high and there were concerns about a poor harvest in the producing areas, they did not offer excessively low prices and maintained their position.

Dried and Fresh Goods Sichuan Suffers Drought, Vegetable Seeds Not Yet Planted, Sichuan Pickled Mustard Suddenly Rises by 5 Yuan 187

Due to severe drought in the Sichuan pickled mustard producing areas, seeds have not yet been planted, which is bound to affect future harvests. Therefore, prices suddenly rose sharply, increasing by as much as 5 yuan. Upon hearing the news, local merchants were greatly excited. Shapai Leqi mustard was offered at 27.50 yuan, and Fuling mustard was offered at 23 yuan, with a total of 400 to 500 jars sold. Inventory was scarce. On the road, Shangpai Hongliyuan Leqi mustard was quoted at 28 to 29 yuan, and market prices also rose by 4 to 5 yuan. Leqi mustard was sold at 24 yuan, and Fuling mustard was sold at 20 yuan.

Silk and Tea Overseas Silk Market Prices Rise, Chinese Silk Sales Expected to be Active 188

Yesterday, the overseas silk market saw a boost as the New York election results were announced, and Mr. Roosevelt was re-elected as president. The exchange market atmosphere was quite invigorated, and the silk industry also followed suit. Near-term contracts rose by 0.05 yuan, and long-term contracts rose by 0.03 yuan. The total transaction volume for the day was 2,570 dan. The Yokohama silk market also rose rapidly, with spot goods rising by 20 yuan and current goods rising by 19 yuan. The local silk market also recovered. Although market prices did not improve, Mitsui and other firms had strong purchasing intentions. The silk market is expected to gradually become active. Yesterday, a total of 265 bales of domestic and foreign silk were sold in the local market.

Tea Merchants' Zhenmei Tea from Fujian Still Sells Well 189

Yesterday, in the foreign tea market, Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi was still selling well. Xiehe Jinlong and other firms made scattered purchases based on telegrams from overseas to Shanghai. Fine needle tea was also continuously replenished. The total transaction volume of various green teas in the city was over 700 boxes. The market price of fine needle tea with good body was slightly firm, while the rest remained flat.

Seafood Kelp and Ribbon Kelp Markets Are Both Firm 190

Kelp: According to telegrams from Hakodate, Qingdao merchants have been purchasing in large quantities at the production area recently, and market prices have gradually risen. Local firms, upon receiving this information, have tightened their sales of existing stock. Furthermore, the supply of new goods is scarce, and sales are strong. Demand from Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and other places is very high, so all grades are in short supply. The current market price for Nemuro medium grade is 11 yuan, Aoba is 10.40 yuan, Maozoku is 9.80 yuan, Niban is 9.20 yuan, and Sanban is 7.20 yuan. The head of the First Bank's price is out of stock, and goods on the road are being sold at 9.80 yuan. All firms are making fixed sales, and the transaction volume is about 1,200 to 1,300 packages.

Ribbon Kelp: Supply is also limited, and the market is stable. (No. 2) Hakodate goods are sold for over 13 yuan, Bai'an goods are sold for 11.50 yuan, and Osaka Shuanglong mark goods have passed through. For next month's futures, foreign firms are selling 300 packages at a price of 10 yuan.
